Kafka will deliver each message in the\n   101→ * subscribed topics to one process in each consumer group. This is achieved by balancing the partitions between all\n   102→ * members in the consumer group so that each partition is assigned to exactly one consumer in the group. So if there\n   103→ * is a topic with four partitions, and a consumer group with two processes, each process would consume from two partitions.\n   104→ * <p>\n   105→ * Membership in a consumer group is maintained dynamically: if a process fails, the partitions assigned to it will\n   106→ * be reassigned to other consumers in the same group. Similarly, if a new consumer joins the group, partitions will be moved\n   107→ * from existing consumers to the new one. This is known as <i>rebalancing</i> the group and is discussed in more\n   108→ * detail <a href=\"#failuredetection\">below</a>. Group rebalancing is also used when new partitions are added\n   109→ * to one of the subscribed topics or when a new topic matching a {@link #subscribe(Pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribed regex}\n   110→ * is created. The group will automatically detect the new partitions through periodic metadata refreshes and\n   111→ * assign them to members of the group.\n   112→ * <p>\n   113→ * Conceptually you can think of a consumer group as being a single logical subscriber that happens to be made up of\n   114→ * multiple processes. As a multi-subscriber system, Kafka naturally supports having any number of consumer groups for a\n   115→ * given topic without duplicating data (additional consumers are actually quite cheap).\n   116→ * <p>\n   117→ * This is a slight generalization of the functionality that is common in messaging systems. To get semantics similar to\n   118→ * a queue in a traditional messaging system all processes would be part of a single consumer group and hence record\n   119→ * delivery would be balanced over the group like with a queue. Unlike a traditional messaging system, though, you can\n   120→ * have multiple such groups. To get semantics similar to pub-sub in a traditional messaging system each process would\n   121→ * have its own consumer group, so each process would subscribe to all the records published to the topic.\n   122→ * <p>\n   123→ * In addition, when group reassignment happens automatically, consumers can be notified through a {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener},\n   124→ * which allows them to finish necessary application-level logic such as state cleanup, manual offset\n   125→ * commits, etc. See <a href=\"#rebalancecallback\">Storing Offsets Outside Kafka</a> for more details.\n   126→ * <p>\n   127→ * It is also possible for the consumer to <a href=\"#manualassignment\">manually assign</a> specific partitions\n   128→ * (similar to the older \"simple\" consumer) using {@link #assign(Collection)}. In this case, dynamic partition\n   129→ * assignment and consumer group coordination will be disabled.\n   130→ *\n   131→ * <h3><a name=\"failuredetection\">Detecting Consumer Failures</a></h3>\n   132→ *\n   133→ * After subscribing to a set of topics, the consumer will automatically join the group when {@link #poll(Duration)} is\n   134→ * invoked. The poll API is designed to ensure consumer liveness. As long as you continue to call poll, the consumer\n   135→ * will stay in the group and continue to receive messages from the partitions it was assigned. Underneath the covers,\n   136→ * the consumer sends periodic heartbeats to the server. If the consumer crashes or is unable to send heartbeats for\n   137→ * a duration of {@code session.timeout.ms}, then the consumer will be considered dead and its partitions will\n   138→ * be reassigned.\n   139→ * <p>\n   140→ * It is also possible that the consumer could encounter a \"livelock\" situation where it is continuing\n   141→ * to send heartbeats, but no progress is being made. To prevent the consumer from holding onto its partitions\n   142→ * indefinitely in this case, we provide a liveness detection mechanism using the {@code max.poll.interval.ms}\n   143→ * setting. Basically if you don't call poll at least as frequently as the configured max interval,\n   144→ * then the client will proactively leave the group so that another consumer can take over its partitions. When this happens,\n   145→ * you may see an offset commit failure (as indicated by a {@link CommitFailedException} thrown from a call to {@link #commitSync()}).\n   146→ * This is a safety mechanism which guarantees that only active members of the group are able to commit offsets.\n   147→ * So to stay in the group, you must continue to call poll.\n   148→ * <p>\n   149→ * The consumer provides two configuration settings to control the behavior of the poll loop:\n   150→ * <ol>\n   151→ *     <li><code>max.poll.interval.ms</code>: By increasing the interval between expected polls, you can give\n   152→ *     the consumer more time to handle a batch of records returned from {@link #poll(Duration)}. The drawback\n   153→ *     is that increasing this value may delay a group rebalance since the consumer will only join the rebalance\n   154→ *     inside the call to poll. You can use this setting to bound the time to finish a rebalance, but\n   155→ *     you risk slower progress if the consumer cannot actually call {@link #poll(Duration) poll} often enough.</li>\n   156→ *     <li><code>max.poll.records</code>: Use this setting to limit the total records returned from a single\n   157→ *     call to poll. This can make it easier to predict the maximum that must be handled within each poll\n   158→ *     interval. By tuning this value, you may be able to reduce the poll interval, which will reduce the\n   159→ *     impact of group rebalancing.</li>\n   160→ * </ol>\n   161→ * <p>\n   162→ * For use cases where message processing time varies unpredictably, neither of these options may be sufficient.\n   163→ * The recommended way to handle these cases is to move message processing to another thread, which allows\n   164→ * the consumer to continue calling {@link #poll(Duration) poll} while the processor is still working.\n   165→ * Some care must be taken to ensure that committed offsets do not get ahead of the actual position.\n   166→ * Typically, you must disable automatic commits and manually commit processed offsets for records only after the\n   167→ * thread has finished handling them (depending on the delivery semantics you need).\n   168→ * Note also that you will need to {@link #pause(Collection) pause} the partition so that no new records are received\n   169→ * from poll until after thread has finished handling those previously returned.\n   170→ *\n   171→ * <h3>Usage Examples</h3>\n   172→ * The consumer APIs offer flexibility to cover a variety of consumption use cases. significant migration from the legacy high-level consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the modern KafkaConsumer API. This analysis examines the implementations and behavioral differences in offset management across the current Kafka and Camel repositories.\\n\\nKAFKA NEW CONSUMER API IMPLEMENTATIONS:\\n\\nThe modern Kafka consumer API is defined by the Consumer interface (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which provides a standardized contract for consuming messages. The primary implementation is KafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which serves as the main public API for consumers.\\n\\nInternally, Kafka uses two delegate implementations:\\n\\n1. ClassicKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides the classic group protocol implementation for backward compatibility with pre-KIP 848 deployments.\\n\\n2. AsyncKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides a newer event-based asynchronous implementation.\\n\\nOFFSET MANAGEMENT IN NEW API:\\n\\nThe new KafkaConsumer API manages offsets through several key mechanisms:\\n\\n1. OffsetAndMetadata (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java) - Encapsulates committed offset positions along with optional metadata.\\n\\n2. CommitRequestManager (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) - Handles offset commit requests in the async implementation. It manages both automatic and manual commits, supporting commitOffsetsAsync() and commitOffsetsSync() methods with proper error handling and callbacks.\\n\\n3. ConsumerCoordinator (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java) - In the classic implementation, coordinates with the broker's group coordinator to manage offset commits.\\n\\nKEY BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCES IN OFFSET MANAGEMENT:\\n\\nLegacy ConsumerConnector API (not found in current repositories - indicates complete migration):\\n- Used simpler offset management through ZooKeeper coordination\\n- Less explicit control over commit semantics\\n- Offset commits were tied to message consumption directly\\n\\nNew KafkaConsumer API:\\n- EXPLICIT OFFSET MANAGEMENT: Offsets must be explicitly tracked and committed via commitSync() or commitAsync() methods\\n- AUTOMATIC VS MANUAL: Configuration option enable.auto.commit controls whether the consumer automatically commits offsets periodically (controlled by auto.commit.interval.ms) or requires manual commits\\n- OFFSET STORAGE: Offsets are stored in Kafka broker topics (__consumer_offsets) rather than ZooKeeper\\n- CALLBACK SUPPORT: commitAsync() accepts OffsetCommitCallback for asynchronous error handling\\n- REBALANCE SEMANTICS: Manual commit calls are tied to consumer group rebalancing - CommitFailedException is thrown if a rebalance occurs during commit\\n- POSITION TRACKING: The consumer maintains both current position (next record to fetch) and committed position (last successfully processed offset)\\n\\nCAMEL KAFKA COMPONENT ADAPTATION:\\n\\nApache Camel provides a wrapper layer around the Kafka consumer API through its KafkaConsumer component (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), which uses the new Kafka Consumer API internally.\\n\\nCommit Manager Strategy Pattern (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManager.java):\\n- CommitManager interface defines the contract for offset commit strategies\\n- AbstractCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) provides base functionality\\n\\nImplementations:\\n\\n1. SyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/SyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitSync() for synchronous offset commits\\n   - Wraps offsets in OffsetAndMetadata with explicit +1 offset calculation\\n   - Blocks until broker acknowledges the commit\\n   - Supports optional StateRepository for persisting offset state\\n   - Calculates timeout from configuration (commitTimeoutMs)\\n\\n2. AsyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AsyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitAsync() for non-blocking offset commits\\n   - Maintains OffsetCache for tracking pending commits\\n   - Provides postCommitCallback() for handling commit completion asynchronously\\n   - Supports offset repository persistence in callback\\n   - More suitable for high-throughput scenarios\\n\\n3. NoopCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/NoopCommitManager.java):\\n   - No-op implementation for scenarios where offset management is disabled\\n\\nMIGRATION SUMMARY:\\n\\nThe migration from ConsumerConnector to KafkaConsumer represents a shift from implicit, ZooKeeper-based offset management to explicit, Kafka broker-based offset management. The new API provides:\\n- More explicit control over when and how offsets are committed\\n- Support for both synchronous and asynchronous commit patterns\\n- Better error handling through exceptions and callbacks\\n- Cleaner separation between current position and committed position\\n- Integration with consumer groups through group coordination\\n\\nThe Camel framework demonstrates how to adapt these APIs into higher-level abstractions, providing multiple commit strategy implementations that allow applications to choose between synchronous reliability and asynchronous throughput.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":365,"cache_read_input_tokens":65819,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":365},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"233bcfe7-8dab-4e1a-8287-52b76a026395","uuid":"f692e949-86a6-4c9f-b2ff-5c7604fe8a1e"}

significant migration from the legacy high-level consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the modern KafkaConsumer API. This analysis examines the implementations and behavioral differences in offset management across the current Kafka and Camel repositories.\\n\\nKAFKA NEW CONSUMER API IMPLEMENTATIONS:\\n\\nThe modern Kafka consumer API is defined by the Consumer interface (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which provides a standardized contract for consuming messages. The primary implementation is KafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which serves as the main public API for consumers.\\n\\nInternally, Kafka uses two delegate implementations:\\n\\n1. ClassicKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides the classic group protocol implementation for backward compatibility with pre-KIP 848 deployments.\\n\\n2. AsyncKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides a newer event-based asynchronous implementation.\\n\\nOFFSET MANAGEMENT IN NEW API:\\n\\nThe new KafkaConsumer API manages offsets through several key mechanisms:\\n\\n1. OffsetAndMetadata (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java) - Encapsulates committed offset positions along with optional metadata.\\n\\n2. CommitRequestManager (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) - Handles offset commit requests in the async implementation. It manages both automatic and manual commits, supporting commitOffsetsAsync() and commitOffsetsSync() methods with proper error handling and callbacks.\\n\\n3. ConsumerCoordinator (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java) - In the classic implementation, coordinates with the broker's group coordinator to manage offset commits.\\n\\nKEY BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCES IN OFFSET MANAGEMENT:\\n\\nLegacy ConsumerConnector API (not found in current repositories - indicates complete migration):\\n- Used simpler offset management through ZooKeeper coordination\\n- Less explicit control over commit semantics\\n- Offset commits were tied to message consumption directly\\n\\nNew KafkaConsumer API:\\n- EXPLICIT OFFSET MANAGEMENT: Offsets must be explicitly tracked and committed via commitSync() or commitAsync() methods\\n- AUTOMATIC VS MANUAL: Configuration option enable.auto.commit controls whether the consumer automatically commits offsets periodically (controlled by auto.commit.interval.ms) or requires manual commits\\n- OFFSET STORAGE: Offsets are stored in Kafka broker topics (__consumer_offsets) rather than ZooKeeper\\n- CALLBACK SUPPORT: commitAsync() accepts OffsetCommitCallback for asynchronous error handling\\n- REBALANCE SEMANTICS: Manual commit calls are tied to consumer group rebalancing - CommitFailedException is thrown if a rebalance occurs during commit\\n- POSITION TRACKING: The consumer maintains both current position (next record to fetch) and committed position (last successfully processed offset)\\n\\nCAMEL KAFKA COMPONENT ADAPTATION:\\n\\nApache Camel provides a wrapper layer around the Kafka consumer API through its KafkaConsumer component (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), which uses the new Kafka Consumer API internally.\\n\\nCommit Manager Strategy Pattern (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManager.java):\\n- CommitManager interface defines the contract for offset commit strategies\\n- AbstractCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) provides base functionality\\n\\nImplementations:\\n\\n1. SyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/SyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitSync() for synchronous offset commits\\n   - Wraps offsets in OffsetAndMetadata with explicit +1 offset calculation\\n   - Blocks until broker acknowledges the commit\\n   - Supports optional StateRepository for persisting offset state\\n   - Calculates timeout from configuration (commitTimeoutMs)\\n\\n2. AsyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AsyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitAsync() for non-blocking offset commits\\n   - Maintains OffsetCache for tracking pending commits\\n   - Provides postCommitCallback() for handling commit completion asynchronously\\n   - Supports offset repository persistence in callback\\n   - More suitable for high-throughput scenarios\\n\\n3. NoopCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/NoopCommitManager.java):\\n   - No-op implementation for scenarios where offset management is disabled\\n\\nMIGRATION SUMMARY:\\n\\nThe migration from ConsumerConnector to KafkaConsumer represents a shift from implicit, ZooKeeper-based offset management to explicit, Kafka broker-based offset management. The new API provides:\\n- More explicit control over when and how offsets are committed\\n- Support for both synchronous and asynchronous commit patterns\\n- Better error handling through exceptions and callbacks\\n- Cleaner separation between current position and committed position\\n- Integration with consumer groups through group coordination\\n\\nThe Camel framework demonstrates how to adapt these APIs into higher-level abstractions, providing multiple commit strategy implementations that allow applications to choose between synchronous reliability and asynchronous throughput.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

significant migration from the legacy high-level consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the modern KafkaConsumer API. This analysis examines the implementations and behavioral differences in offset management across the current Kafka and Camel repositories.\\n\\nKAFKA NEW CONSUMER API IMPLEMENTATIONS:\\n\\nThe modern Kafka consumer API is defined by the Consumer interface (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java), which provides a standardized contract for consuming messages. The primary implementation is KafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which serves as the main public API for consumers.\\n\\nInternally, Kafka uses two delegate implementations:\\n\\n1. ClassicKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides the classic group protocol implementation for backward compatibility with pre-KIP 848 deployments.\\n\\n2. AsyncKafkaConsumer (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) - implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> and provides a newer event-based asynchronous implementation.\\n\\nOFFSET MANAGEMENT IN NEW API:\\n\\nThe new KafkaConsumer API manages offsets through several key mechanisms:\\n\\n1. OffsetAndMetadata (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java) - Encapsulates committed offset positions along with optional metadata.\\n\\n2. CommitRequestManager (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) - Handles offset commit requests in the async implementation. It manages both automatic and manual commits, supporting commitOffsetsAsync() and commitOffsetsSync() methods with proper error handling and callbacks.\\n\\n3. ConsumerCoordinator (apache/kafka: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java) - In the classic implementation, coordinates with the broker's group coordinator to manage offset commits.\\n\\nKEY BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCES IN OFFSET MANAGEMENT:\\n\\nLegacy ConsumerConnector API (not found in current repositories - indicates complete migration):\\n- Used simpler offset management through ZooKeeper coordination\\n- Less explicit control over commit semantics\\n- Offset commits were tied to message consumption directly\\n\\nNew KafkaConsumer API:\\n- EXPLICIT OFFSET MANAGEMENT: Offsets must be explicitly tracked and committed via commitSync() or commitAsync() methods\\n- AUTOMATIC VS MANUAL: Configuration option enable.auto.commit controls whether the consumer automatically commits offsets periodically (controlled by auto.commit.interval.ms) or requires manual commits\\n- OFFSET STORAGE: Offsets are stored in Kafka broker topics (__consumer_offsets) rather than ZooKeeper\\n- CALLBACK SUPPORT: commitAsync() accepts OffsetCommitCallback for asynchronous error handling\\n- REBALANCE SEMANTICS: Manual commit calls are tied to consumer group rebalancing - CommitFailedException is thrown if a rebalance occurs during commit\\n- POSITION TRACKING: The consumer maintains both current position (next record to fetch) and committed position (last successfully processed offset)\\n\\nCAMEL KAFKA COMPONENT ADAPTATION:\\n\\nApache Camel provides a wrapper layer around the Kafka consumer API through its KafkaConsumer component (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), which uses the new Kafka Consumer API internally.\\n\\nCommit Manager Strategy Pattern (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManager.java):\\n- CommitManager interface defines the contract for offset commit strategies\\n- AbstractCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java) provides base functionality\\n\\nImplementations:\\n\\n1. SyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/SyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitSync() for synchronous offset commits\\n   - Wraps offsets in OffsetAndMetadata with explicit +1 offset calculation\\n   - Blocks until broker acknowledges the commit\\n   - Supports optional StateRepository for persisting offset state\\n   - Calculates timeout from configuration (commitTimeoutMs)\\n\\n2. AsyncCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AsyncCommitManager.java):\\n   - Uses consumer.commitAsync() for non-blocking offset commits\\n   - Maintains OffsetCache for tracking pending commits\\n   - Provides postCommitCallback() for handling commit completion asynchronously\\n   - Supports offset repository persistence in callback\\n   - More suitable for high-throughput scenarios\\n\\n3. NoopCommitManager (apache/camel: components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/NoopCommitManager.java):\\n   - No-op implementation for scenarios where offset management is disabled\\n\\nMIGRATION SUMMARY:\\n\\nThe migration from ConsumerConnector to KafkaConsumer represents a shift from implicit, ZooKeeper-based offset management to explicit, Kafka broker-based offset management. The new API provides:\\n- More explicit control over when and how offsets are committed\\n- Support for both synchronous and asynchronous commit patterns\\n- Better error handling through exceptions and callbacks\\n- Cleaner separation between current position and committed position\\n- Integration with consumer groups through group coordination\\n\\nThe Camel framework demonstrates how to adapt these APIs into higher-level abstractions, providing multiple commit strategy implementations that allow applications to choose between synchronous reliability and asynchronous throughput.\"\n}\n","numLines":42,"startLine":1,"totalLines":42}}}
